<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<section class="tab-pane pure-u-1-1 u-printing-display-inline-ie u-printing-display-inline-ff">
		<!-- ngIf: vm.loading -->
		<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading --><div ng-if="!vm.loading" class="ng-scope">
			<!-- uiView: --><div ui-view="" class="ng-scope"><section class="pure-u-1-1 document-abstract document-tab u-p-2 ng-isolate-scope" mathjax-bind="" id="6153042">

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1' : 'pure-u-1-1'" class="ng-scope pure-u-1-1">
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">Passive and semipassive UHF RF identification (RFID) systems have traditionally been designed using scalar-valued differential radar cross section (DRCS) methods to model the backscattered signal from the tag. This paper argues that scalar-valued DRCS analysis is unnecessarily limiting because of the inherent coherence of the backscatter link and the complex-valued nature of load-dependent antenna-mode scattering from an RFID tag. Considering modulated backscatter in terms of complex-valued scattered fields opens the possibility of quadrature modulation of the backscatter channel. When compared with binary amplitude shift keying (ASK) or phase shift keying (PSK) based RFID systems, which transmit 1 bit of data per symbol period, and thus 1 bit per on-chip clock oscillator period, tags employing vector backscatter modulation can transmit more than 1 bit per symbol period. This increases the data rate for a given on-chip symbol clock rate leading to reduced on-chip power consumption and extended read range. Alternatively, tags employing an M-ary modulator can achieve log<sub>2</sub> M higher data throughput at essentially the same dc power consumption as a tag employing binary ASK or PSK. In contrast to the binary ASK or PSK backscatter modulation employed by passive and semipassive UHF RFID tags, such as tags compliant with the widely used ISO18000-6c standard, this paper explores a novel CMOS-compatible method for generating M-ary quadrature amplitude modulated (QAM) backscatter modulation. A new method is presented for designing an inductorless M-ary QAM backscatter modulator using only an array of switched resistances and capacitances. Device-level simulation and measurements of a four-state phase shift keying (4-PSK)/four-state quadrature amplitude modulated (4-QAM) modulator are provided for a semipassive (battery-assisted) tag operating in the 850-950-MHz band. This first prototype modulator transmits 4-PSK/4-QAM at a symbol rate of 200 kHz and a bit rate of 400 kb/s at a static power dissipation of only 115 nW.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->
		</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Ultra-High frequency (UHF) RF identification (RFID) systems employing modulated backscatter communication links, such as those based on the widely deployed ISO18000-6c or EPC Global Class 1 Generation 2 specification <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, have traditionally been analyzed using techniques first developed to analyze radar systems. This paper demonstrates that scalar valued differential radar cross section (DRCS) techniques are unnecessarily limiting for RFID system analysis because of the inherent coherence of the backscatter link and the complex-valued nature of load-dependent scattering from an RFID tag's antenna.</p><p>In most commonly deployed UHF RFID systems, the UHF backscatter link employs a simple binary modulation scheme, such as amplitude shift keying (ASK) or phase shift keying (PSK) backscatter generated by a two-state modulation of the impedance presented to a transponder's antenna (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>). Since tag to reader distance is generally unknown <i>a priori</i>, most readers employ homodyne in-phase/quadrature (I/Q) demodulation and rotate the received constellation until it falls on the real axis before demodulating as if the signal were ASK regardless of whether the tag's modulator is configured to generate ASK or PSK modulation. In this paper, we exploit multistate complex-valued load-dependent scattering to yield quadrature amplitude modulated (QAM) backscatter that is compatible with the homodyne reader architecture.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Typical UHF RFID system with binary load modulation yielding ASK or PSK binary demodulated signal.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>This paper, an expanded version of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, demonstrates the use of load-dependent scattering to generate QAM backscatter with a simple modulator suitable for single-chip CMOS implementation. The modulator presented in this study has a static power consumption of only 115 nW. Related work has presented a vector modulator based on a p-i-n diode phase shifter controlled by bias currents generated by two digital-to-analog converters (DACs) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. The latter circuit has a static power consumption of 80 mW, which is prohibitively high power consumption for either passive or semipassive tags. In contrast to the present approach, it is not suitable for monolithic implementation because p-i-n diodes and wideband quadrature hybrids are not available in standard CMOS processes.</p><p>The use of QAM in passive and semipassive UHF RFID opens up many new avenues for UHF RFID, including higher spectral efficiency than is possible with ASK or PSK and improved data throughput with reduced on-chip symbol clock rate.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Scalar-Valued Radar Cross Section (RCS) in RFID System Analysis</h2></div><p>For a monostatic radar illuminating an uncooperative target, such as an aircraft or a ship, the reflected energy from the target is often estimated using the target's scalar RCS. Scalar RCS in this context is simply a measure of the target's structural scattering at a particular attitude with respect to the radar. RCS is defined in terms of incident and scattered fields <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="display: inline-block; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-164" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-169" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BB.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the radar's wavelength.</p><p>Unlike a typically uncooperative radar target, the goal of a passive or semipassive UHF RFID transponder or âtagâ is to communicate information to the reader by modulated backscatter through a mutually agreed modulation and data format. The backscattered field consists of structural scattering, which is not intentionally modulated, as well as load-dependent scattering that is modulated with data by varying the impedance presented by the tag circuit to the tag's antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. It has been shown that careful load selection can be used to maximize the backscattered field amplitude, as discussed in early backscatter work <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>, as well as in modern UHF RFID systems <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>. A typical CMOS implementation of a binary PSK modulator, showing the switched modulating capacitance, appears in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig><p>Example PSK modulation circuit typical of current generation RFID tags. <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Complex-Valued Scattered Fields</h2></div><p>Hansen <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_3">[10]</a> previously analyzed a special case of radar scattering where the scatterer is an antenna connected to a load. This work relates Hansen's scattering results to the UHF RFID context and extends it to multiple load impedance states.</p><p>The reflected field from a tag can be decomposed into structural scattering and load-dependent scattering terms <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-425" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -1.318em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: 0.003em; border-top: 1.3px solid; width: 2.946em; height: 0px;"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 1.084em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-618" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 3px; height: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.898em 1001.14em 0.423em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.14em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(8)}}$" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-550" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-551" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-552" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-553" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-555" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0028.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0038.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0029.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.997em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 2.537em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-27">\Delta E_{\rm scat} = (\Gamma ^{\ast }_{1} - \Gamma ^{\ast }_{2}) {{E_{\rm ant} I^{\ast }_{m}}\over {I_{\rm ant}}}. \eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\Delta E_{\rm scat} = (\Gamma ^{\ast }_{1} - \Gamma ^{\ast }_{2}) {{E_{\rm ant} I^{\ast }_{m}}\over {I_{\rm ant}}}. \eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span></span></disp-formula> In contrast to the traditional DRCS of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5-6" href="#deqn5-6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a> that yields only scalar results, the differential <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-619" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-620" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-621" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0045.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-field scattering is a vector that, when demodulated, may occupy any quadrant of the I/Q plane. The critical observation is that applying carefully selected loads to the antenna will result in the scattered <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-622" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-623" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0045.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-field exhibiting amplitude modulation, phase modulation, or both simultaneously and independently yielding a QAM constellation.</p><p>In the simplest implementation, an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-625" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-626" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-627" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-ary QAM modulation scheme can be implemented with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-628" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-629" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-630" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distinct load impedances that are switched across the terminals of the tag's antenna, although other implementations are possible, including a simple impedance (DAC) where weighted arrays of inductors, capacitors, and resistors are used to reduce the number of lumped elements to fewer than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-631" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-632" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In a monolithic implementation this translates to a reduction in die area, and thus a cost and yield improvement. For many types of antennas, it is possible to design such an impedance DAC with only resistors and capacitors, which makes the approach particularly suitable for CMOS integration.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Demodulation in Passive and Semipassive UHF RFID Systems</h2></div><p>Current passive and semipassive RFID tag modulators are designed either to modulate the real part of the tag integrated circuit's (IC)'s reflection coefficient, yielding ASK backscatter, or the imaginary part, yielding PSK backscatter. The most common circuit implementation of ASK for passive devices switches between a matched state, which maximizes power delivered to the passive tag's power rectifier circuitry, and a load resistance that introduces a deliberate mismatch to produce a backscatter signal. A binary PSK modulation circuit is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> where the modulating transistor switches a capacitance across the antenna's terminals to introduce a phase shift in the scattered field.</p><p>Since typical RFID readers employ homodyne receivers, the backscatter link is coherent to the reader's transmit local oscillator. Due to this coherence, the phase of the backscatter, as observed in the demodulated baseband, changes with tag to reader distance. As the tag moves radially outward from a reader, the phase of the backscatter field incident on the receiver rotates at a rate of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-634" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.144em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-635" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-636" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-637" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03C0.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">2 \pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> radians per half-wavelength of distance. At the 860â950-MHz frequencies typically used for UHF RFID, this leads to a rotation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-638" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.144em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-639" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-640" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-641" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03C0.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">2\pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> every <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-642" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 3.847em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.426em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.43em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-643" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-644" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/2248.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-645" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-646" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-647" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-648" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-649" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0036.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0020.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0063.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">\approx {\hbox {16 cm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Since the reader to tag distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-650" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.483em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-651" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-652" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0072.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">r</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is usually initially unknown and both ASK and PSK modulation schemes are permitted by most RFID standards <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_4">[1]</a>, the reader must be able to demodulate tag signals arriving at any phase. For binary modulation schemes such as ASK or PSK, the reader's baseband signal processing software typically rotates the received signal vector from its arrival angle in the I/Q plane back to the in-phase axis prior to data slicing to demodulate the tag's binary data. Most existing RFID reader hardware is therefore not restricted to binary ASK/PSK backscatter modulation. While upgraded reader baseband signal processing software would be required to demodulate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-653" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-654" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-655" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-ary QAM data with some increase in computational complexity, QAM demodulation is supported by the existing RFID reader architecture.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Received Signals in the Presence of Multipath and Tag Motion</h2></div><p>The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-656" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-657" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-658" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0045.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; In contrast, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(c)</a>, changing the tag-to-reader separation distance rotates total scattered field <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1114" role="math" style="display: inline-block; In the multipath case, as well as the moving-tag case, there is a fixed phase relationship between the structural scattering and antenna-mode scattering, which is desirable because it preserves the transmitted constellation.</p><p>This model has been confirmed experimentally through measurements described below.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>QAM Tag Modulator Design and Simulation</h2></div><p>Based on the observation from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> that a careful choice of modulating load impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1129" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1250" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1251" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03B1.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\alpha</script></tex-math></inline-formula> closer to 1 reflect increasing amounts of the incident RF power back to the reader and thus result in higher backscatter signal strength. This is the typical case for a semipassive (battery-assisted) tag, such as the one described in this study, because maximizing the backscatter signal strength gives the longest read range. Passive tags, however, must harvest their dc operating power from the incident field. Values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1252" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.946em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1253" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1254" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03B1.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1255" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/226A.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 15px; height: 10px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1256" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">\alpha \ll 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are typical for a passive tag to permit a majority of the incident field to be absorbed in the energy harvesting circuit. Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1257" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.664em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1258" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1259" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03B1.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.603em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">\alpha</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a constant that relates power reflection and power transmission coefficients, the optimal value will depend on the desired balance between backscattered signal power and power delivered to the energy harvesting circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_6">[11]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_6">[12]</a>. For binary ASK and PSK, this tradeoff has previously been analyzed as a function of reflection coefficient <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_6">[13]</a>. Due to government regulations limiting the reader's transmitted power, well-designed passive RFID systems usually operate in a forward-link limited regime where the read distance is limited by the ability to deliver power to the tag.</p><p>By rearranging the conjugate reflection coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1260" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Experimental Validation</h3><p>Based on the block diagram in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>, a discrete component semipassive tag pictured in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> was constructed to test a 4-PSK/4-QAM backscatter modulator designed with this procedure. Four lumped impedances are connected to an antenna port through an Analog Devices ADG904 single-pole four-throw (SP4T) CMOS field-effect transistor (FET) switch that is controlled by a TI MSP430F2011 microcontroller. The microcontroller was programmed to stream 128-bit strings of pseudorandom data to modulate the four switch states at 200-k symbols/s, corresponding to a data rate of 400 kb/s. The static dc power consumption of the modulator, excluding the power consumption of the microcontroller, is 3.0 V at 38.3 nA, or 115 nW. The dynamic power consumption is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. In the prototype tag, a MSP430F2011 microcontroller consumes an additional 1â2 mA (or 3â6 mW) when generating the pseudorandom data. A CR2032 3-V lithium coin cell battery serves as a power source for the device.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Block diagram of the 4-PSK/4-QAM semipassive tag. In this modulator implementation, the number of discrete impedance states is equal to the number of symbols.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">+{\hbox{3 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 915 MHz was used as the forward link source. The reflected signal was separated using a MiniCircuits ZFDC-15-10 15-dB directional coupler and fed to a Linear Technology LT5575 I/Q demodulator. The baseband I and Q signals were sampled at 8-bit resolution with a sampling rate of 2 MS/s using an Agilent Infinium DSO8104 oscilloscope. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9(a)</a> shows the received constellation generated by the L&amp;C modulator, while <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9(b)</a> shows the received constellation generated by the C-Only modulator as captured by the oscilloscope with random I and Q data.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig><p>Measured I/Q baseband constellations (density plot) generated by the semipassive tag in the cabled test setup. (a) 4-QAM/4-PSK (L &amp; C). (b) 4-QAM/4-PSK (C-Only).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Digitally generated additive white Gaussian noise (AWGN) was summed with the captured time-domain signal samples. A minimum distance soft decision demodulator was used to obtain BER curves for the two constellations (L&amp;C, and C-Only) found in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TablesÂ I</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">II</a> and the Smith charts of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. The resulting measured BER curves, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>, showed good agreement with those predicted by Matlab simulation.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 10. </b><fig><p>Simulation versus cabled setup measurement of BER for 4-QAM/4-PSK modulation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The final step was to connect the switched impedances to a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1785" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1786" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1787" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/03A9.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dipole antenna and perform an over-the-air test of the resulting semipassive backscatter modulator. The transmitter employed for this test consisted of an Agilent MXG N5181A synthesized signal source followed by a Mini-Circuits ZHL-5W-2G amplifier yielding a conducted output power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1788" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 4.267em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.847em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.85em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1789" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1790" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002B.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1791" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1792" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1793" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1794" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1795" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0033.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0020.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0042.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">+{\hbox{30 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) of this transmitter setup was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1796" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 5.108em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.568em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.57em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1797" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1798" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002B.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1799" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1800" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1801" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1802" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1803" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0033.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0038.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 3px; height: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0034.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0020.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0042.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">+{\hbox{38.4 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> given a Yagi antenna of 9-dBi gain and a cable loss of 0.6 dB. A 6-dBi patch receiving antenna was located with close proximity to the transmitting antenna to minimize the radar bistatic angle. The test setup used for gathering the over-the-air data is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig><p>Test setup for over-the-air measurements.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>As the tag moved radially outward with respect to the reader, the baseband constellation was observed to rotate and scale as expected given the signal model presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>. Due to the indoor environment and the interaction with multipath signals, some locations in the laboratory exhibited a deep fade in the detected backscatter signal. This behavior is typical for any passive or semipassive backscatter system and is not specific to the QAM modulation method presented in this study.</p><p>During initial testing in a typical indoor laboratory environment, 500Â 000 bits were transmitted from multiple locations. No more than 1-bit error was observed at any location within 4.5 m. This implies a BER of less than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1804" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 3.246em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1002.89em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1805" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1806" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/2248.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 7px; vertical-align: 1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1807" style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1808" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1809" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1810" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1811" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1812" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1813" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1814" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1815" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/2212.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 1px; vertical-align: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1816" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0035.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">\approx {\hbox{10}}^{-5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> over the air in a low-interference relatively controlled laboratory setting. Given the experimental setup, measurement times, and thus the number of bits accumulated for error rate measurements, are limited by oscilloscope capture memory depth. The tag was then fixed at a separation of 2.92 m from the transmit antenna and the RF power feeding the antenna was swept to produce the data shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>. Simulation as well as over-the-air results show the C-Only 4-QAM/4-PSK constellation performance trailed the L&amp;C performance by a margin of approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1817" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 3.667em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1818" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1819" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002B.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1820" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1821" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1822" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1823" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1824" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 3px; height: 2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0035.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0020.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 0px; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.243em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0064.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0042.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">+{\hbox {1.5 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> Eb/N0 to achieve equivalent BER. This is a tradeoff due to the reduction in inter-symbol distance brought about by the compression of the C-Only constellation by the factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1825" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.604em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.54em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1826" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1827" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03B2.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\beta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6176247/6153042/6153042-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 12. </b><fig><p>Measured and simulated over-the-air BER versus Eb/N0 in an indoor environment for 4-QAM/4-PSK implemented with both inductors and capacitors (L&amp;C), as well as capacitors only (C-Only).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6153042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Discussion</h2></div><p>The development of passive and semipassive RFID system models has, in most cases, followed directly from radar systems techniques. While scalar valued DRCS analysis is useful for analyzing binary ASK or PSK modulation schemes, the DRCS approach is unnecessarily limiting. Since the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1828" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1829" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1830" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0045.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-field scattered from a tag antenna is complex valued, passive and semipassive RFID systems can be designed to produce <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1831" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1832" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1833" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-ary QAM signals with minimal increase in cost or complexity at the tag or the reader.</p><p>More versatile <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1834" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1835" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1836" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-ary modulation schemes also permit an important new design space for RFID systems. Since a tag's on-chip oscillator frequency ultimately limits the symbol rate, not the bit rate, higher values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1837" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1838" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1839" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> yield increased data rate for a given on-chip oscillator frequency. This, in turn, allows for fine-grained tradeoffs between on-chip power consumption, data rate, and link margin.</p><p>In terms of bandwidth (spectral) efficiency and performance in the presence of AWGN, 4-QAM/4-PSK and binary PAM have equivalent performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_7">[15]</a>. For a given data rate, the lower symbol rate of 4-QAM/4-PSK permits the QAM modulator transistors to switch at half the frequency compared to a binary modulator. In general, an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1840" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1841" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1842" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/004D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 16px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-ary QAM modulator can be clocked slower by a factor of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1843" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1844" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1845" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.2em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1846" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; In the digital sections of a tag IC, careful choice of internal memory bus width, and associated data path width may also allow the clock rate driving these on-chip circuits to be correspondingly reduced. The power dissipation in all of these sections will thus decrease in accordance with the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1852" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Higher order constellations can improve modulator power efficiency further.</p><p>As an example, a 16-QAM constellation is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a> for implementation either with or without inductors. When designed for a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1874" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Future modulator designs can be realized with weighted combinations of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1917" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec8"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VIII.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Device-level simulation and measurements of a 4-PSK/4-QAM modulator are presented for a semipassive (battery-assisted) tag operating in the 850â950-MHz band. This first prototype modulator consumes a static power of only 115 nW, but is capable of transmitting 4-PSK/4-QAM data at a rate of 200-k symbols/s or 400 kb/s. The measured power consumption shows a linear increase in modulator power as the data rate increases, as expected from the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1932" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 5.288em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1004.75em 2.586em -999.997em); height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1940" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1941" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1942" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1949" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1950" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1951" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1952" style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-137">{({1}/ {2})}CV^{2}f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> power dissipation model for CMOS switching devices. While power consumption increased with the symbol rate due to the switching devices used in the prototype, it remained insignificant when compared to the consumption levels of the low-power Texas Instruments Incorporated MSP430 microcontroller.</p><p>When compared with binary ASK- or PSK-based RFID systems, tags employing vector backscatter modulation hold the promise of higher data throughput while running at a lower on-chip clock frequency, thereby reducing on-chip power consumption and extending read range. Alternatively, tags employing an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1954" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>

Semipassive UHF RFID Systems","abstract":"Passive and semipassive UHF RF identification (RFID) systems have traditionally been designed using scalar-valued differential radar cross section (DRCS) methods to model the backscattered signal from the tag. This paper argues that scalar-valued DRCS analysis is unnecessarily limiting because of the inherent coherence of the backscatter link and the complex-valued nature of load-dependent antenna-mode scattering from an RFID tag. Considering modulated backscatter in terms of complex-valued scattered fields opens the possibility of quadrature modulation of the backscatter channel. When compared with binary amplitude shift keying (ASK) or phase shift keying (PSK) based RFID systems, which transmit 1 bit of data per symbol period, and thus 1 bit per on-chip clock oscillator period, tags employing vector backscatter modulation can transmit more than 1 bit per symbol period. This increases the data rate for a given on-chip symbol clock rate leading to reduced on-chip power consumption and extended read range. Alternatively, tags employing an M-ary modulator can achieve log&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; M higher data throughput at essentially the same dc power consumption as a tag employing binary ASK or PSK. In contrast to the binary ASK or PSK backscatter modulation employed by passive and semipassive UHF RFID tags, such as tags compliant with the widely used ISO18000-6c standard, this paper explores a novel CMOS-compatible method for generating M-ary quadrature amplitude modulated (QAM) backscatter modulation. A new method is presented for designing an inductorless M-ary QAM backscatter modulator using only an array of switched resistances and capacitances. Device-level simulation and measurements of a four-state phase shift keying (4-PSK)/four-state quadrature amplitude modulated (4-QAM) modulator are provided for a semipassive (battery-assisted) tag operating in the 850-950-MHz band. This first prototype modulator transmits 4-PSK/4-QAM at a symbol rate of 200 kHz and a bit rate of 400 kb/s at a static power dissipation of only 115 nW.","doi":"10.1109/TMTT.2012.2185810","startPage":"1175","publicationTitle":"IEEE Transactions on Microwave Theory and Techniques","endPage":"1182","isJournal":true,"isConference":false,"dateOfInsertion":"03 April 2012","publisher":"IEEE","accessionNumber":"12638291","htmlLink":"/document/6153042/","isEarlyAccess":false,"isBook":false,"isEphemera":false,"isOpenAccess":false,"isSMPTE":false,"journalDisplayDateOfPublication":"15 February 2012","chronOrPublicationDate":"April  2012","isFreeDocument":false,"isCustomDenial":false,"persistentLink":"http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=22","isStaticHtml":true,"isNotDynamicOrStatic":false,"htmlAbstractLink":"/document/6153042/","isPromo":false,"isDynamicHtml":true,"isStandard":false,"publicationDate":"April 2012","conferenceDate":" ","isACM":false,"issue":"4","volume":"60","startPage":"1175","openAccessFlag":"no","ephemeraFlag":"false","title":"Quadrature Amplitude Modulated Backscatter in Passive and Semipassive UHF RFID Systems","confLoc":"","accessionNumber":"12638291","ml_html_flag":"true","html_flag":"true","content_type":"Journals &amp;
